# Attributes:
#	ID: 6 digits identification number
#		A######: HornMorpho ِoriginal entry (A: Amharic, G: Ge'ez, R: Tigrinya, T: Tigre)
#		K######: Kalmasoft added entry
#	Ethiopic: Ethiopic entry
#	ETIPA: Reading for Ethiopic entry (International Phonetic Alphabet)
#	ARIPA: Reading for Arabic (International Phonetic Alphabet)
#	Arabic: Arabic parallel word
#	ETClass/ARClass: Ethiopic/Arabic grammatical class
#		A: Adjective
#		D: Adverb
#		I: Infinitive (Amharic infinitive, Arabic Mimatic infinitive)
#		G: Gerund (Amharic gerund)
#		M: Masdar (Arabic infinitive)
#		N: Noun
#		NT: Arabic Temporal noun
#		NL: Arabic Locative noun
#		Ncol [CC]: Regional colloquial Arabic Noun, ISO3166-3 Alpha-2 country codes, apply only to MSA otherwise
#		R: Particle
#		P: Participle (Amharic and Arabic active participle)
#		Vcol [CC]: Regional colloquial Arabic Verb, ISO3166-3 Alpha-2 country codes, apply only to MSA otherwise
#		VI: Verb imperfective (Amharic contingent, Arabic imperfective)
#		VC: Verb compound imperfective (Amharic compound imperfective, Arabic emphatic imperfective)
#		VJ: Verb jussive
#		VM: Verb imperative
#		VP: Verb perfective
#	ETSubclass/ARSubclass: Ethiopic/Arabic entry grammatical subclass
#		CON: Conjunction
#		PRP: Preposition
#		SNG: Singular
#		PLR: Plural
#		ACC: Accusative case
#		NOM: Nominative case
#		DAT: Dative case
#		GEN: Genitive case
#		IND: Indicative mood
#		SUB: Subjunctive mood
#	ETDomain/ARDomain: Ethiopic/Arabic entry semantic domain
#		ANAT: Anatomy
#		ANIM: Animate
#		DMST: Domestic
#		DATE: Date
#		LANG: Language specific
#		NAME: Named entity
#		NUMB: Number
#		PLNT: Plant
#		RLGN: Religion
#	Category: Arabic entry usage category
#		ARC: Ethiopic archaic entry
#		FFM: full form morphology
#		NUS: not used in Arabic
#		SSH: semantically shifted in Arabic
#	RootET: Ethiopic theoretical root
#	RootAR: Arabic root
#	Language: Ethiopic language, ISO 639-3 three-letter code
#	Gloss: English meaning of the Ethiopic entry
# ================================================================================================

A00660	ጨርቅ	/tʃɛrɨkʼ/	/χiraq/	خِرَق	N	N	SNG	SNG	DMST	DMST			خرق	amh	Rag, n. 1 a a torn, frayed, or worn piece of woven material. b one of the irregular scraps to which cloth etc. is reduced by wear and tear. 2 (in pl.) old or worn clothes. 3 (collect.) scraps of cloth used as material for paper, stuffing, etc. 4 derog. a a newspaper. b a flag, handkerchief, curtain, etc. 5 (usu. with neg.) the smallest scrap of cloth etc. (not a rag to cover him). 6 an odd scrap; an irregular piece. 7 a jagged projection, esp. on metal. in rags 1 much torn. 2 in old torn clothes. rag-and-bone man Brit. an itinerant dealer in old clothes, furniture, etc. rag-bag 1 a bag in which scraps of fabric etc. are kept for use. 2 a miscellaneous collection. 3 sl. a sloppily-dressed woman. rag bolt a bolt with barbs to keep it tight when it has been driven in. rag book a children''s book made of untearable cloth. rag doll a stuffed doll made of cloth. rag paper paper made from rags. rag-picker a collector and seller of rags. rags to riches poverty to affluence. rag trade colloq. the business of designing, making, and selling women''s clothes.
